<table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <img alt="" data-file-height="235" data-file-width="323" height="29" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Farsi.svg/40px-Farsi.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Farsi.svg/60px-Farsi.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Farsi.svg/80px-Farsi.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">\n         <b>\n          This article contains\n          <a href="/wiki/Persian_alphabet" title="Persian alphabet">\n           Persian text\n          </a>\n          .\n         </b>\n         Without proper\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:Arabic" title="Help:Arabic">\n          rendering support\n         </a>\n         , you may see\n         <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">\n          question marks, boxes, or other symbols\n         </a>\n         .\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Persian\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">\n            p\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r/: \'ur\' in \'fur\'">\n            \xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xca\x92/: \'s\' in \'pleasure\'">\n            \xca\x92\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99n/: \'on\' in \'button\'">\n            \xc9\x99n\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       or\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">\n            p\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r/: \'ur\' in \'fur\'">\n            \xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xca\x83/: \'sh\' in \'shy\'">\n            \xca\x83\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99n/: \'on\' in \'button\'">\n            \xc9\x99n\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ), also known by its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endonym" title="Endonym">\n        endonym\n       </a>\n       <b>\n        Farsi\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span lang="fa" xml:lang="fa">\n        \xd9\x81\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb3\xdb\x8c\n       </span>\n       <i>\n        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="fa ALA transliteration">\n         f\xc4\x81rsi\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Persian" title="Help:IPA/Persian">\n         [f\xc9\x92\xcb\x90\xc9\xbe\xcb\x88si\xcb\x90]\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <small class="nowrap">\n        (\n        <span class="unicode haudio">\n         <span class="fn">\n          <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n           <a href="/wiki/File:Farsi.ogg" title="About this sound">\n            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>\n           </a>\n          </span>\n          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8e/Farsi.ogg" title="Farsi.ogg">\n           listen\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        )\n       </small>\n       ), is one of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Iranian_languages" title="Western Iranian languages">\n        Western Iranian languages\n       </a>\n       within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indo-Iranian_languages" title="Indo-Iranian languages">\n        Indo-Iranian branch\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">\n        Indo-European language family\n       </a>\n       . It is primarily spoken in\n       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">\n        Iran\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">\n        Afghanistan\n       </a>\n       (officially known as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Dari_language" title="Dari language">\n         Dari\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       since 1958),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">\n        Tajikistan\n       </a>\n       (officially known as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">\n         Tajiki\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       since the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">\n        Soviet\n       </a>\n       era),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and some other regions which historically were\n       <a href="/wiki/Persianate_society" title="Persianate society">\n        Persianate societies\n       </a>\n       and considered part of\n       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Iran" title="Greater Iran">\n        Greater Iran\n       </a>\n       . It is written in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_alphabet" title="Persian alphabet">\n        Persian alphabet\n       </a>\n       , a modified variant of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">\n        Arabic script\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Persian language is classified as a continuation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Persian" title="Middle Persian">\n        Middle Persian\n       </a>\n       , the official religious and literary language of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">\n        Sasanian Empire\n       </a>\n       , itself a continuation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Old_Persian" title="Old Persian">\n        Old Persian\n       </a>\n       , the language of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">\n        Achaemenid Empire\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lazard_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lazard-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Its grammar is similar to that of many contemporary European languages.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richard_Davis_2006._pp._602-603_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Richard_Davis_2006._pp._602-603-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Persian gets its name from its origin at the capital of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">\n        Achaemenid Empire\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Persis" title="Persis">\n        Persis\n       </a>\n       (modern-day\n       <a href="/wiki/Fars_Province" title="Fars Province">\n        Fars Province\n       </a>\n       ), hence the name Persian (\n       <i>\n        Farsi\n       </i>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A Persian-speaking person may be referred to as\n       <i>\n        Persophone\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are approximately 110 million Persian speakers worldwide, with the language holding official status in\n       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">\n        Iran\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">\n        Afghanistan\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">\n        Tajikistan\n       </a>\n       . For centuries, Persian has also been a prestigious cultural language in other regions of\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">\n        Western Asia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">\n        Central Asia\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">\n        South Asia\n       </a>\n       by the various empires based in the regions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Persian_literature_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Persian_literature-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Persian has had a considerable (mainly\n       <a href="/wiki/Lexicon" title="Lexicon">\n        lexical\n       </a>\n       ) influence on neighboring languages, particularly the\n       <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">\n        Turkic languages\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">\n        Central Asia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">\n        Caucasus\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">\n        Anatolia\n       </a>\n       , neighboring Iranian languages, as well as\n       <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">\n        Armenian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">\n        Georgian\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">\n        Indo-Aryan languages\n       </a>\n       , especially\n       <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">\n        Urdu\n       </a>\n       (a register of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_language" title="Hindustani language">\n        Hindustani\n       </a>\n       ). It also exerted some influence on\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       , particularly\n       <a href="/wiki/Bahrani_Arabic" title="Bahrani Arabic">\n        Bahrani Arabic\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       while borrowing much vocabulary from it after the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_conquest_of_Iran" title="Arab conquest of Iran">\n        Arab conquest of Iran\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lazard_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lazard-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richard_Davis_2006._pp._602-603_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Richard_Davis_2006._pp._602-603-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lazard.2C_Gilbert_1971_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lazard.2C_Gilbert_1971-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nushin_Namazi_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Nushin_Namazi-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Classe_2000_1057_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Classe_2000_1057-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lambtonexcerpt_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lambtonexcerpt-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With a long history of literature in the form of Middle Persian before Islam, Persian was the first language in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">\n        Muslim world\n       </a>\n       to break through\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       \'s monopoly on writing, and the writing of poetry in Persian was established as a court tradition in many eastern courts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Persian_literature_16-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Persian_literature-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some of the famous works of\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_literature" title="Persian literature">\n        Persian literature\n       </a>\n       are the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Shahnameh" title="Shahnameh">\n         Shahnameh\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ferdowsi" title="Ferdowsi">\n        Ferdowsi\n       </a>\n       , the works of\n       <a href="/wiki/Rumi" title="Rumi">\n        Rumi\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rubaiyat_of_Omar_Khayyam" title="Rubaiyat of Omar Khayyam">\n        <i>\n         Rubaiyat\n        </i>\n        of Omar Khayyam\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khamsa_of_Nizami" title="Khamsa of Nizami">\n         Panj Ganj\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Nizami_Ganjavi" title="Nizami Ganjavi">\n        Nizami Ganjavi\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <i>\n        Div\xc4\x81n\n       </i>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hafez" title="Hafez">\n        Hafez\n       </a>\n       and the two miscellanea of prose and verse by\n       <a href="/wiki/Saadi_Shirazi" title="Saadi Shirazi">\n        Saadi Shirazi\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Gulistan_(book)" title="Gulistan (book)">\n         Gulistan\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Bustan_(book)" title="Bustan (book)">\n         Bustan\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#Examples">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Examples\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">\n        Classification\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Classification">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Persian is one of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Iranian_languages" title="Western Iranian languages">\n        Western Iranian languages\n       </a>\n       within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">\n        Indo-European family\n       </a>\n       . Other Western Iranian languages are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_languages" title="Kurdish languages">\n        Kurdish languages\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gilaki_language" title="Gilaki language">\n        Gilaki\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mazanderani_language" title="Mazanderani language">\n        Mazanderani\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Talysh_language" title="Talysh language">\n        Talysh\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Balochi_language" title="Balochi language">\n        Balochi\n       </a>\n       . Persian is classified as a member of the Southwestern subgroup within Western Iranian along with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lari_language" title="Lari language">\n        Lari\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kumzari_language" title="Kumzari language">\n        Kumzari\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Luri_language" title="Luri language">\n        Luri\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-windfuhr1987_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-windfuhr1987-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">\n        Etymology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Persian_language_name_in_Persian">\n        Persian language name in Persian\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Persian language name in Persian">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In Persian, the language is known by several names:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Western_Persian" title="Western Persian">\n          Western Persian\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ,\n        <i>\n         Parsi\n        </i>\n        (\n        <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n         \xd9\xbe\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb3\xdb\x8c\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x80\x8e\n        <i>\n         <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Persian transliteration">\n          p\xc4\x81rsi\n         </span>\n        </i>\n        ) or\n        <i>\n         Farsi\n        </i>\n        (\n        <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n         \xd9\x81\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb3\xdb\x8c\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x80\x8e\n        <i>\n         <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Persian transliteration">\n          f\xc4\x81rsi\n         </span>\n        </i>\n        or\n        <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n         \xd8\xb2\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd9\x81\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb3\xdb\x8c\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x80\x8e\n        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Persian transliteration">\n         <i>\n          zab\xc4\x81n-e f\xc4\x81rsi\n         </i>\n        </span>\n        ) has been the name used by all native speakers until the 20th century. In recent decades some authors writing in English have referred to the variety of Persian spoken in Iran as\n        <i>\n         Farsi\n        </i>\n        ;\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n         <a href="#cite_note-24">\n          [24]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n         <a href="#cite_note-25">\n          [25]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        although the name\n        <i>\n         Persian\n        </i>\n        is also still widely used.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n         <a href="#cite_note-26">\n          [26]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n         <a href="#cite_note-27">\n          [27]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n         <a href="#cite_note-28">\n          [28]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Persian" title="Eastern Persian">\n         Eastern Persian\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Dari_language" title="Dari language">\n          Dari Persian\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        (\n        <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', IranNastaliq, \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Nastaliq">\n         \xd8\xaf\xd8\xb1\xdb\x8c\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x80\x8e\n        <i>\n         <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Dari transliteration">\n          dar\xc4\xab\n         </span>\n        </i>\n        or\n        <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', IranNastaliq, \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Nastaliq">\n         \xd9\x81\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb3\xdb\x8c \xd8\xaf\xd8\xb1\xdb\x8c\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x80\x8e\n        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Dari transliteration">\n         <i>\n          f\xc4\x81rsi-ye dari\n         </i>\n        </span>\n        ) was originally a synonym for\n        <i>\n         F\xc4\x81rsi\n        </i>\n        but since the latter decades of the 20th century has become the name for the variety of Persian spoken in\n        <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">\n         Afghanistan\n        </a>\n        , where it is one of the two official languages; it is sometimes called\n        <i>\n         Afghan Persian\n        </i>\n        in English.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n         <a href="#cite_note-29">\n          [29]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">\n          Tajiki\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        (\n        <span lang="tg-Cyrl" xml:lang="tg-Cyrl">\n         \xd1\x82\xd0\xbe\xd2\xb7\xd0\xb8\xd0\xba\xd3\xa3\n        </span>\n        ,\n        <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', IranNastaliq, \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Nastaliq">\n         \xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd8\xac\xdb\x8c\xda\xa9\xdb\x8c\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x80\x8e\n        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Tajik transliteration">\n         <i>\n          tojik\xc4\xab\n         </i>\n        </span>\n        or\n        <span lang="tg-Cyrl" xml:lang="tg-Cyrl">\n         \xd0\xb7\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbe\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb8 \xd1\x82\xd0\xbe\xd2\xb7\xd0\xb8\xd0\xba\xd3\xa3\n        </span>\n        /\n        <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', IranNastaliq, \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Nastaliq">\n         \xd9\x81\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb3\xdb\x8c \xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd8\xac\xdb\x8c\xda\xa9\xdb\x8c\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x80\x8e\n        <i>\n         <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Tajik transliteration">\n          zabon-i tojiki\n         </span>\n        </i>\n        ) is the variety of Persian spoken in\n        <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">\n         Tajikistan\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">\n         Uzbekistan\n        </a>\n        by the\n        <a href="/wiki/Tajiks" title="Tajiks">\n         Tajiks\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Persian_language_name_in_English">\n        Persian language name in English\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Persian language name in English">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Persian\n       </i>\n       , the historically more widely used name of the language in\n       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">\n        English\n       </a>\n       , is an anglicized form derived from\n       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">\n        Latin\n       </a>\n       *\n       <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n        <i>\n         Persianus\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       &lt; Latin\n       <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n        <i>\n         Persia\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       &lt;\n       <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">\n        Greek\n       </a>\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        \xce\xa0\xce\xb5\xcf\x81\xcf\x83\xce\xaf\xcf\x82\n        <i>\n         Pers\xc3\xads\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       "Persia",\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       a Hellenized form of Old Persian\n       <span lang="peo-Latn" xml:lang="peo-Latn">\n        <i>\n         P\xc4\x81rsa\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">\n         Oxford English Dictionary\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , the term\n       <i>\n        Persian\n       </i>\n       as a language name is first attested in English in the mid-16th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Native Iranian Persian speakers call it\n       <i>\n        F\xc4\x81rsi\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED_Farsi_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OED_Farsi-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Farsi\n       </i>\n       is the Arabicized form of\n       <i>\n        P\xc4\x81rsi\n       </i>\n       , subsequent to\n       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia" title="Muslim conquest of Persia">\n        Muslim conquest of Persia\n       </a>\n       , due to a lack of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">\n        phoneme\n       </a>\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /p/\n       </span>\n       in Standard Arabic (i.e., the\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /p/\n       </span>\n       was replaced with an\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /f/\n       </span>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spooner1994_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Spooner1994-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spooner2012_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Spooner2012-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CWL2013_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CWL2013-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The origin of the name\n       <i>\n        Farsi\n       </i>\n       and the place of origin of the language which is\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Fars_Province" title="Fars Province">\n         Fars Province\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       is the Arabicized form of\n       <i>\n        P\xc4\x81rs\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spooner1994_34-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Spooner1994-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spooner2012_35-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Spooner2012-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CWL2013_36-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CWL2013-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In English, this language has historically been known as\n       <i>\n        Persian\n       </i>\n       , though\n       <i>\n        Farsi\n       </i>\n       has also gained some currency.\n       <i>\n        Farsi\n       </i>\n       is encountered in some linguistic literature as a name for the language, used both by Iranian and by foreign authors.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In modern English the word\n       <i>\n        Farsi\n       </i>\n       refers to the language while\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Parsi" title="Parsi">\n         Parsi\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (or\n       <i>\n        Parsee\n       </i>\n       ) describes\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoroastrians" title="Zoroastrians">\n        Zoroastrians\n       </a>\n       , particularly in South Asia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Persian_Language_and_Literature" title="Academy of Persian Language and Literature">\n        Academy of Persian Language and Literature\n       </a>\n       has declared that the name\n       <i>\n        Persian\n       </i>\n       is more appropriate, as it has the longer tradition in western languages and better expresses the role of the language as a mark of cultural and national continuity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some Persian language scholars such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Ehsan_Yarshater" title="Ehsan Yarshater">\n        Ehsan Yarshater\n       </a>\n       , editor of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Iranica" title="Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Iranica">\n         Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Iranica\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arizona" title="University of Arizona">\n        University of Arizona\n       </a>\n       professor\n       <a href="/wiki/Kamran_Talattof" title="Kamran Talattof">\n        Kamran Talattof\n       </a>\n       , have also rejected the usage of "Farsi" in their articles.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The international language-encoding standard\n       <a href="/wiki/ISO_639-1" title="ISO 639-1">\n        ISO 639-1\n       </a>\n       uses the code\n       <code>\n        fa\n       </code>\n       , as its coding system is mostly based on the local names. The more detailed standard\n       <a href="/wiki/ISO_639-3" title="ISO 639-3">\n        ISO 639-3\n       </a>\n       uses the name "Persian" (code\n       <code>\n        fas\n       </code>\n       ) for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">\n        dialect continuum\n       </a>\n       spoken across Iran and Afghanistan. This consists of the individual languages\n       <a href="/wiki/Dari_language" title="Dari language">\n        Dari\n       </a>\n       (Afghan Persian) and Iranian Persian.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Currently,\n       <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">\n        Voice of America\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">\n        BBC World Service\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Welle" title="Deutsche Welle">\n        Deutsche Welle\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty" title="Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty">\n        Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty\n       </a>\n       use "Persian Service" for their broadcasts in the language. Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty also includes a Tajik service and an Afghan (Dari) service. This is also the case for the\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=American_Association_of_Teachers_of_Persian&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="American Association of Teachers of Persian (page does not exist)">\n        American Association of Teachers of Persian\n       </a>\n       , The Centre for Promotion of Persian Language and Literature, and many of the leading scholars of the Persian language.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table cellpadding="3" cellspacing="0" style="margin: 0 0 1em 1em; border: 1px solid #aaa; background: #fff; font-size:90%; float:right; clear:right">\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center;background:#ccf;">\n         <big>\n          <b>\n           <a href="/wiki/Persian_language#History" title="Persian language">\n            History of the\n            <br/>\n            Persian language\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </big>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center;">\n         <b>\n          <a href="/wiki/Proto-Iranian_language" title="Proto-Iranian language">\n           Proto-Iranian\n          </a>\n         </b>\n         (c. 1500 BCE)\n         <p>\n          <small>\n           <a href="/wiki/Western_Iranian_languages" title="Western Iranian languages">\n            Western Iranian languages\n           </a>\n          </small>\n         </p>\n         <hr/>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center;">\n         <b>\n          <a href="/wiki/Old_Persian" title="Old Persian">\n           Old Persian\n          </a>\n         </b>\n         (c. 525 \xe2\x80\x93 300 BCE)\n         <p>\n          <small>\n           <a href="/wiki/Old_Persian_cuneiform" title="Old Persian cuneiform">\n            Old Persian cuneiform\n           </a>\n          </small>\n         </p>\n         <hr/>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center;">\n         <b>\n          <a href="/wiki/Middle_Persian" title="Middle Persian">\n           Middle Persian\n          </a>\n         </b>\n         (c. 300 BCE \xe2\x80\x93 800 CE)\n         <p>\n          <small>\n           <a href="/wiki/Pahlavi_scripts" title="Pahlavi scripts">\n            Pahlavi scripts\n           </a>\n          </small>\n          \xe2\x80\xa2\n          <small>\n           <a href="/wiki/Manichaean_alphabet" title="Manichaean alphabet">\n            Manichaean alphabet\n           </a>\n          </small>\n          \xe2\x80\xa2\n          <small>\n           <a href="/wiki/Avestan_alphabet" title="Avestan alphabet">\n            Avestan alphabet\n           </a>\n          </small>\n         </p>\n         <hr/>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center;">\n         <b>\n          <a class="mw-selflink selflink">\n           Modern Persian\n          </a>\n         </b>\n         (from 800)\n         <p>\n          <small>\n           <a href="/wiki/Persian_alphabet" title="Persian alphabet">\n            Persian alphabet\n           </a>\n          </small>\n          \xe2\x80\xa2\n          <small>\n           <a href="/wiki/Tajik_alphabet#Cyrillic" title="Tajik alphabet">\n            Tajiki Cyrillic alphabet\n           </a>\n          </small>\n         </p>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Persian is an Iranian language belonging to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indo-Iranian_languages" title="Indo-Iranian languages">\n        Indo-Iranian\n       </a>\n       branch of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">\n        Indo-European\n       </a>\n       family of languages. In general, Iranian languages are known from three periods, usually referred to as Old, Middle, and New (Modern) periods. These correspond to three eras in\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iran" title="History of Iran">\n        Iranian history\n       </a>\n       ; Old era being the period from sometime before Achaemenids, the Achaemenid era and sometime after Achaemenids (that is to 400\xe2\x80\x93300 BC), Middle era being the next period most officially Sassanid era and sometime in post-Sassanid era, and the New era being the period afterwards down to present day.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EI-IL-vi_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EI-IL-vi-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to available documents, the Persian language is "the only Iranian language"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lazard_10-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lazard-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       for which close philological relationships between all of its three stages are established and so that Old, Middle, and New Persian represent\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lazard_10-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lazard-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EI-IL-vi.282.29_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EI-IL-vi.282.29-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       one and the same language of Persian; that is, New Persian is a direct descendant of Middle and Old Persian.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EI-IL-vi.282.29_44-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EI-IL-vi.282.29-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The known history of the Persian language can be divided into the following three distinct periods:\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Persian">\n        Old Persian\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Old Persian">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Old_Persian" title="Old Persian">\n        Old Persian\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_verbs" title="Persian verbs">\n        Persian verbs\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pers%C3%A9polis._Inscription.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1107" data-file-width="1675" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pers%C3%A9polis._Inscription.jpg/250px-Pers%C3%A9polis._Inscription.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pers%C3%A9polis._Inscription.jpg/375px-Pers%C3%A9polis._Inscription.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pers%C3%A9polis._Inscription.jpg/500px-Pers%C3%A9polis._Inscription.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pers%C3%A9polis._Inscription.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Old_Persian" title="Old Persian">\n          Old Persian\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As a\n       <a href="/wiki/Written_language" title="Written language">\n        written language\n       </a>\n       , Old Persian is attested in royal\n       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">\n        Achaemenid\n       </a>\n       inscriptions. The oldest known text written in Old Persian is from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Behistun_Inscription" title="Behistun Inscription">\n        Behistun Inscription\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-s2008-80-1_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-s2008-80-1-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Examples of Old Persian have been found in what is now\n       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">\n        Iran\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">\n        Romania\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Gherla" title="Gherla">\n        Gherla\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhrt2013197_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhrt2013197-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrye1984103_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrye1984103-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt200053_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt200053-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">\n        Armenia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">\n        Bahrain\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">\n        Iraq\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">\n        Turkey\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">\n        Egypt\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OPGTL_6_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OPGTL_6-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Old Persian is one of the oldest Indo-European languages which is attested in original texts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EI-IL-vi-vi.282.29_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EI-IL-vi-vi.282.29-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Xenophon" title="Xenophon">\n        Xenophon\n       </a>\n       , a Greek general serving in some of the Persian expeditions, describes many aspects of Armenian village life and hospitality in around 401 BC, which is at a time when Old Persian was the only form of Persian used. He relates that the\n       <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">\n        Armenians\n       </a>\n       spoke a language that to his ear sounded like the language of the Persians.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Persian">\n        Middle Persian\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Middle Persian">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Persian" title="Middle Persian">\n        Middle Persian\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The complex\n       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_conjugation" title="Grammatical conjugation">\n        grammatical conjugation\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Declension" title="Declension">\n        declension\n       </a>\n       of Old Persian yielded to the structure of Middle Persian in which the dual number disappeared, leaving only singular and plural, as did gender. Middle Persian developed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ez%C4%81fe" title="Ez\xc4\x81fe">\n        ez\xc4\x81fe\n       </a>\n       construction, expressed through\n       <i>\n        \xc4\xab\n       </i>\n       (modern\n       <i>\n        ye\n       </i>\n       ), to indicate some of the relations between words that have been lost with the simplification of the earlier grammatical system.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although the "middle period" of the Iranian languages formally begins with the fall of the Achaemenid Empire, the transition from Old to Middle Persian had probably already begun before the 4th century. However, Middle Persian is not actually attested until 600 years later when it appears in the Sassanid era (224\xe2\x80\x93651) inscriptions, so any form of the language before this date cannot be described with any degree of certainty. Moreover, as a literary language, Middle Persian is not attested until much later, to the 6th or 7th century. And from the 8th century onward, Middle Persian gradually began yielding to New Persian, with the middle-period form only continuing in the texts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">\n        Zoroastrianism\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The native name of Middle Persian was\n       <i>\n        Parsig\n       </i>\n       or\n       <i>\n        Parsik\n       </i>\n       , after the name of the ethnic group of the southwest, that is, "of\n       <i>\n        Pars\n       </i>\n       ", Old Persian\n       <i>\n        Parsa\n       </i>\n       , New Persian\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Fars_Province" title="Fars Province">\n         Fars\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . This is the origin of the name\n       <i>\n        Farsi\n       </i>\n       as it is today used to signify New Persian. Following the collapse of the Sassanid state,\n       <i>\n        Parsik\n       </i>\n       came to be applied exclusively to (either Middle or New) Persian that was written in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">\n        Arabic script\n       </a>\n       . From about the 9th century onward, as Middle Persian was on the threshold of becoming New Persian, the older form of the language came to be erroneously called\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Middle_Persian" title="Middle Persian">\n         Pahlavi\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , which was actually but one of the\n       <i>\n        writing systems\n       </i>\n       used to render both Middle Persian as well as various other Middle Iranian languages. That writing system had previously been adopted by the Sassanids (who were Persians, i.e. from the southwest) from the preceding Arsacids (who were Parthians, i.e. from the northeast). While\n       <a href="/wiki/Ibn_al-Muqaffa%27" title="Ibn al-Muqaffa\'">\n        Ibn al-Muqaffa\'\n       </a>\n       (eighth century) still distinguished between\n       <i>\n        Pahlavi\n       </i>\n       (i.e. Parthian) and\n       <i>\n        Persian\n       </i>\n       (in Arabic text: al-Farisiyah) (i.e. Middle Persian), this distinction is not evident in Arab commentaries written after that date.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Gernot Windfuhr considers new Persian as an evolution of the Old Persian language and the Middle Persian language\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but also states that none of the known Middle Persian dialects is the direct predecessor of Modern Persian.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ludwig Paul states: "The language of the Shahnameh should be seen as one instance of continuous historical development from Middle to New Persian."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="New_Persian">\n        New Persian\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: New Persian">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rudaba.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="908" data-file-width="595" height="397" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Rudaba.JPG/260px-Rudaba.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Rudaba.JPG/390px-Rudaba.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Rudaba.JPG/520px-Rudaba.JPG 2x" width="260"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rudaba.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ferdowsi" title="Ferdowsi">\n          Ferdowsi\n         </a>\n         \'s\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Shahnameh" title="Shahnameh">\n           Shahnameh\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       "New Persian" is conventionally divided into three stages:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Early New Persian (8th/9th centuries)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Classical Persian (10th\xe2\x80\x9318th centuries)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Contemporary Persian (19th century to present)\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Early New Persian remains largely intelligible to speakers of Contemporary Persian, as the morphology and, to a lesser extent, the lexicon of the language have remained relatively stable.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_New_Persian">\n        Early New Persian\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Early New Persian">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       "New Persian" is taken to replace Middle Persian in the course of the 8th to 9th centuries, under\n       <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">\n        Abbasid rule\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-turkiclanguages.com_58-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-turkiclanguages.com-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With the decline of the Abbasids began the reestablishment of Persian national life and Persians laid the foundations for a renaissance in the realm of letters. New Persian as an independent literary language first emerges in\n       <a href="/wiki/Bactria" title="Bactria">\n        Bactria\n       </a>\n       through the adaptation of the spoken form of Sassanian Middle Persian court language called\n       <a href="/wiki/Dari_language" title="Dari language">\n        Dari\n       </a>\n       . The cradle of the Persian literary renaissance lay in the east of\n       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Iran" title="Greater Iran">\n        Greater Iran\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Khorasan" title="Greater Khorasan">\n        Greater Khorasan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Transoxiana" title="Transoxiana">\n        Transoxiana\n       </a>\n       close to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Amu_Darya" title="Amu Darya">\n        Amu Darya\n       </a>\n       (Modern day Afghanistan).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Public_Domain_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Public_Domain-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The mastery of the newer speech having now been transformed from Middle into New Persian was already complete by the era of the three princely dynasties of Iranian origin, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tahirid_dynasty" title="Tahirid dynasty">\n        Tahirid dynasty\n       </a>\n       (820\xe2\x80\x93872),\n       <a href="/wiki/Saffarid_dynasty" title="Saffarid dynasty">\n        Saffarid dynasty\n       </a>\n       (860\xe2\x80\x93903) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Samanid_Empire" title="Samanid Empire">\n        Samanid Empire\n       </a>\n       (874\xe2\x80\x93999), and could develop only in range and power of expression.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Public_Domain_59-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Public_Domain-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Abbas of\n       <a href="/wiki/Merv" title="Merv">\n        Merv\n       </a>\n       is mentioned as being the earliest minstrel to chant verse in the newer Persian tongue and after him the poems of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hanzala_Badghisi" title="Hanzala Badghisi">\n        Hanzala Badghisi\n       </a>\n       were among the most famous between the Persian-speakers of the time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first poems of the Persian language, a language historically called Dari, emerged in Afghanistan.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adamec_61-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Adamec-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first significant Persian poet was\n       <a href="/wiki/Rudaki" title="Rudaki">\n        Rudaki\n       </a>\n       . He flourished in the 10th century, when the Samanids were at the height of their power. His reputation as a court poet and as an accomplished musician and singer has survived, although little of his poetry has been preserved. Among his lost works is versified fables collected in the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Panchatantra" title="Panchatantra">\n         Kalila wa Dimna\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Persian_literature_16-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Persian_literature-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The language spread geographically from the 11th century on and was the medium through which among others, Central Asian Turks became familiar with Islam and urban culture. New Persian was widely used as a trans-regional\n       <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">\n        lingua franca\n       </a>\n       , a task for which it was particularly suitable due to its relatively simple morphological structure and this situation persisted until at least 19th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-turkiclanguages.com_58-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-turkiclanguages.com-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the late Middle Ages, new Islamic literary languages were created on the Persian model:\n       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">\n        Ottoman Turkish\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_language" title="Chagatai language">\n        Chagatai\n       </a>\n       and Urdu, which are regarded as "structural daughter languages" of Persian.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-turkiclanguages.com_58-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-turkiclanguages.com-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_Persian">\n        Classical Persian\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Classical Persian">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Persian_poets_and_authors" title="List of Persian poets and authors">\n        List of Persian poets and authors\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kalila_wa_Dimna_001.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1118" data-file-width="937" height="310" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Kalila_wa_Dimna_001.jpg/260px-Kalila_wa_Dimna_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Kalila_wa_Dimna_001.jpg/390px-Kalila_wa_Dimna_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Kalila_wa_Dimna_001.jpg/520px-Kalila_wa_Dimna_001.jpg 2x" width="260"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kalila_wa_Dimna_001.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Panchatantra" title="Panchatantra">\n          Kalilah va Dimna\n         </a>\n         , an influential work in Persian literature.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       "Classical Persian" loosely refers to the standardized language of medieval Persia used in\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_literature" title="Persian literature">\n        literature\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persian_poetry" title="Persian poetry">\n        poetry\n       </a>\n       . This is the language of the 10th to 12th centuries, which continued to be used as literary language and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">\n        lingua franca\n       </a>\n       under the "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persianized" title="Persianized">\n        Persianized\n       </a>\n       " Turko-Mongol dynasties during the 12th to 15th centuries, and under restored Persian rule during the 16th to 19th centuries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Persian during this time served as lingua franca of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Persia" title="Greater Persia">\n        Greater Persia\n       </a>\n       and of much of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">\n        Indian subcontinent\n       </a>\n       . It was also the official and cultural language of many Islamic dynasties, including the Samanids,\n       <a href="/wiki/Buyid_dynasty" title="Buyid dynasty">\n        Buyids\n       </a>\n       , Tahirids,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ziyarid_dynasty" title="Ziyarid dynasty">\n        Ziyarids\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">\n        Mughal Empire\n       </a>\n       , Timurids,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ghaznavids" title="Ghaznavids">\n        Ghaznavids\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Seljuq_dynasty" title="Seljuq dynasty">\n        Seljuqs\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Khwarazmian_dynasty" title="Khwarazmian dynasty">\n        Khwarazmians\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum" title="Sultanate of Rum">\n        Sultanate of Rum\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shirvanshah" title="Shirvanshah">\n        Shirvanshahs\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">\n        Safavids\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Afsharid_dynasty" title="Afsharid dynasty">\n        Afsharids\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Zand_dynasty" title="Zand dynasty">\n        Zands\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">\n        Qajars\n       </a>\n       , Ottomans and also many Mughal successors such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nizam_of_Hyderabad" title="Nizam of Hyderabad">\n        Nizam of Hyderabad\n       </a>\n       . Persian was the only non-European language known and used by\n       <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">\n        Marco Polo\n       </a>\n       at the Court of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">\n        Kublai Khan\n       </a>\n       and in his journeys through China.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Use_in_Asia_Minor">\n        Use in Asia Minor\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Use in Asia Minor">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_miniature_painters.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="364" data-file-width="460" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Ottoman_miniature_painters.jpg/260px-Ottoman_miniature_painters.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Ottoman_miniature_painters.jpg/390px-Ottoman_miniature_painters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ef/Ottoman_miniature_painters.jpg 2x" width="260"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_miniature_painters.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Persian on an\n         <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_miniature" title="Ottoman miniature">\n          Ottoman miniature\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Despite\n       <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">\n        Anatolia\n       </a>\n       having been ruled at various times prior to the Middle Ages by various Persian-speaking dynasties originating in Iran, the language lost its traditional foothold there with the demise of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">\n        Sasanian Empire\n       </a>\n       . Centuries later however, the practise and usage of Persian in the region would be strongly revived. A branch of the Seljuks, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum" title="Sultanate of Rum">\n        Sultanate of Rum\n       </a>\n       , took Persian language, art and letters to Anatolia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sigfried_J_1994._p_734_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sigfried_J_1994._p_734-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They adopted Persian language as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">\n        official language\n       </a>\n       of the empire.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Ottomans, which can roughly be seen as their eventual successors, took this tradition over. Persian was the official court language of the empire, and for some time, the official language of the empire.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The educated and noble class of the Ottoman Empire all spoke Persian, such as sultan\n       <a href="/wiki/Selim_I" title="Selim I">\n        Selim I\n       </a>\n       , despite being Safavid Iran\'s archrival and a staunch opposer of\n       <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">\n        Shia Islam\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was a major literary language in the empire.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some of the noted earlier Persian works during the Ottoman rule are\n       <a href="/wiki/Idris_Bitlisi" title="Idris Bitlisi">\n        Idris Bidlisi\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <i>\n        Hasht Bihisht\n       </i>\n       , which begun in 1502 and covered the reign of the first eight Ottoman rulers, and the\n       <i>\n        Salim-Namah\n       </i>\n       , a glorification of Selim I.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_67-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After a period of several centuries, Ottoman Turkish (which was highly Persianised itself) had developed towards a fully accepted language of literature, which was even able to satisfy the demands of a scientific presentation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bertold_Spuler_p_69_69-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bertold_Spuler_p_69-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, the number of Persian and Arabic loanwords contained in those works increased at times up to 88%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bertold_Spuler_p_69_69-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bertold_Spuler_p_69-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Use_in_South_Asia">\n        Use in South Asia\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Use in South Asia">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_language_in_South_Asia" title="Persian language in South Asia">\n        Persian language in South Asia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_and_Urdu" title="Persian and Urdu">\n        Persian and Urdu\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Agra_India_persian_poem.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Agra_India_persian_poem.jpg/220px-Agra_India_persian_poem.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Agra_India_persian_poem.jpg/330px-Agra_India_persian_poem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Agra_India_persian_poem.jpg/440px-Agra_India_persian_poem.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Agra_India_persian_poem.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Persian poem,\n         <a href="/wiki/Agra_Fort" title="Agra Fort">\n          Agra Fort\n         </a>\n         , India, 18th century\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Agra_castle_India_persian_poem.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Agra_castle_India_persian_poem.jpg/220px-Agra_castle_India_persian_poem.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Agra_castle_India_persian_poem.jpg/330px-Agra_castle_India_persian_poem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Agra_castle_India_persian_poem.jpg/440px-Agra_castle_India_persian_poem.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Agra_castle_India_persian_poem.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Persian poem,\n         <i>\n          Takht-e Shah Jahan\n         </i>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Agra_Fort" title="Agra Fort">\n          Agra Fort\n         </a>\n         , India\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Persian language influenced the formation of many modern languages in West Asia, Europe,\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">\n        Central Asia\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">\n        South Asia\n       </a>\n       . Following the Turko-Persian\n       <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_of_Ghazni" title="Mahmud of Ghazni">\n        Ghaznavid\n       </a>\n       conquest of\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">\n        South Asia\n       </a>\n       , Persian was firstly introduced in the region by Turkic Central Asians.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The basis in general for the introduction of Persian language into the subcontinent was set, from its earliest days, by various Persianized Central Asian Turkic and Afghan dynasties.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sigfried_J_1994._p_734_64-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sigfried_J_1994._p_734-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For five centuries prior to the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">\n        British colonization\n       </a>\n       , Persian was widely used as a second language in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">\n        Indian subcontinent\n       </a>\n       , due to the admiration the Mughals (who were of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turco-Mongol" title="Turco-Mongol">\n        Turco-Mongol\n       </a>\n       origin) had for the foreign language. It took prominence as the language of culture and education in several Muslim courts on the subcontinent and became the sole "official language" under the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">\n        Mughal emperors\n       </a>\n       . Beginning in 1843, though,\n       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">\n        English\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_language" title="Hindustani language">\n        Hindustani\n       </a>\n       gradually replaced Persian in importance on the subcontinent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Evidence of Persian\'s historical influence there can be seen in the extent of its influence on certain languages of the Indian subcontinent. Words borrowed from Persian are still quite commonly used in certain Indo-Aryan languages, especially\n       <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">\n        Urdu\n       </a>\n       , also historically known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_language" title="Hindustani language">\n        Hindustani\n       </a>\n       . There is also a small population of Zoroastrian\n       <a href="/wiki/Irani_(India)" title="Irani (India)">\n        Iranis\n       </a>\n       in India, who migrated around 16th-18th century to escape religious execution in\n       <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">\n        Qajar Iran\n       </a>\n       and speak a Dari dialect.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_Persian">\n        Contemporary Persian\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Contemporary Persian">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Persian_keyboard_layout,_unshifted.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="175" data-file-width="525" height="73" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Persian_keyboard_layout%2C_unshifted.gif/220px-Persian_keyboard_layout%2C_unshifted.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Persian_keyboard_layout%2C_unshifted.gif/330px-Persian_keyboard_layout%2C_unshifted.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Persian_keyboard_layout%2C_unshifted.gif/440px-Persian_keyboard_layout%2C_unshifted.gif 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Persian_keyboard_layout,_unshifted.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A variant of the Iranian standard ISIRI 9147 keyboard layout for Persian\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the 19th century, under the\n       <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">\n        Qajar dynasty\n       </a>\n       , the dialect spoken in\n       <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">\n        Tehran\n       </a>\n       rose to prominence. This became the basis of what is now known as "Contemporary Standard Persian".\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is still substantial Arabic vocabulary, but many of these words have been integrated into Persian phonology and grammar. In addition, since the 19th\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       century numerous\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">\n        English\n       </a>\n       terms have been borrowed, especially vocabulary related to technology. The Iranian National\n       <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Persian_Language_and_Literature" title="Academy of Persian Language and Literature">\n        Academy of Persian Language and Literature\n       </a>\n       is responsible for evaluating neologisms in order to devise their Persian equivalents.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Varieties">\n        Varieties\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Varieties">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n
