   </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       There are three modern varieties of standard Persian:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Western_Persian" title="Western Persian">\n          Western Persian\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        (\n        <i>\n         Persian\n        </i>\n        ,\n        <i>\n         Iranian Persian\n        </i>\n        , or\n        <i>\n         Farsi\n        </i>\n        ) is spoken in\n        <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">\n         Iran\n        </a>\n        , and by minorities in\n        <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">\n         Iraq\n        </a>\n        and the\n        <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">\n         Persian Gulf\n        </a>\n        states.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Dari_language" title="Dari language">\n          Dari\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        (\n        <i>\n         Dari Persian\n        </i>\n        ,\n        <i>\n         Afghan Persian\n        </i>\n        , or\n        <i>\n         Dari\n        </i>\n        ) is spoken in\n        <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">\n         Afghanistan\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">\n          Tajiki\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        (\n        <i>\n         Tajik Persian\n        </i>\n        ) is spoken in\n        <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">\n         Tajikistan\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">\n         Uzbekistan\n        </a>\n        . It is written in the\n        <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">\n         Cyrillic script\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       All these three varieties are based on the classic Persian literature and its literary tradition. There are also several local dialects from Iran, Afghanistan and Tajikistan which slightly differ from the standard Persian. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Hazaragi_dialect" title="Hazaragi dialect">\n        Hazaragi dialect\n       </a>\n       (in Central Afghanistan and Pakistan),\n       <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">\n        Herati\n       </a>\n       (in Western Afghanistan), Darwazi (in Afghanistan and Tajikistan), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tehrani_accent" title="Tehrani accent">\n        Tehrani accent\n       </a>\n       (in Iran, the basis of standard Iranian Persian) are examples of these dialects. Persian-speaking peoples of Iran, Afghanistan, and Tajikistan can understand one another with a relatively high degree of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mutual_intelligibility" title="Mutual intelligibility">\n        mutual intelligibility\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The following are some languages closely related to Persian, or in some cases are considered dialects:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Luri_language" title="Luri language">\n         Luri\n        </a>\n        (or\n        <i>\n         Lori\n        </i>\n        ), spoken mainly in the southwestern Iranian provinces of\n        <a href="/wiki/Lorestan_Province" title="Lorestan Province">\n         Lorestan\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Kohgiluyeh_and_Boyer-Ahmad_Province" title="Kohgiluyeh and Boyer-Ahmad Province">\n         Kohgiluyeh and Boyer-Ahmad Province\n        </a>\n        , some western parts of\n        <a href="/wiki/Fars_Province" title="Fars Province">\n         Fars Province\n        </a>\n        and some parts of\n        <a href="/wiki/Khuzestan_Province" title="Khuzestan Province">\n         Khuzestan Province\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lari_language" title="Lari language">\n         Lari\n        </a>\n        (in southern Iran)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Tat_language_(Caucasus)" title="Tat language (Caucasus)">\n         Tat\n        </a>\n        , spoken in parts of Azerbaijan, Russia, and Transcaucasia. It is classified as a variety of Persian.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gernot_Windfuhr_1979._pg_4_73-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Gernot_Windfuhr_1979._pg_4-73">\n          [73]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n         <a href="#cite_note-74">\n          [74]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n         <a href="#cite_note-75">\n          [75]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n         <a href="#cite_note-76">\n          [76]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n         <a href="#cite_note-77">\n          [77]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Judeo-Tat" title="Judeo-Tat">\n         Judeo-Tat\n        </a>\n        . Part of the Tat Persian continuum, and spoken in Azerbaijan, Russia, as well as notably by immigrant communities in Israel and New York.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">\n        Phonology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Phonology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_phonology" title="Persian phonology">\n        Persian phonology\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Iranian Persian has six vowels and twenty-three consonants.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">\n        Vowels\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Vowels">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Farsi_vowel_chart.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="980" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Farsi_vowel_chart.svg/290px-Farsi_vowel_chart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Farsi_vowel_chart.svg/435px-Farsi_vowel_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Farsi_vowel_chart.svg/580px-Farsi_vowel_chart.svg.png 2x" width="290"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Farsi_vowel_chart.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The vowel phonemes of modern Tehran Persian\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Historically, Persian has distinguished length. Early New Persian had a series of five long vowels (\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">\n         i\xcb\x90\n        </a>\n        /\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">\n         u\xcb\x90\n        </a>\n        /\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Open_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open back rounded vowel">\n         \xc9\x92\xcb\x90\n        </a>\n        /\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">\n         o\xcb\x90\n        </a>\n        /\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid front unrounded vowel">\n         e\xcb\x90\n        </a>\n        /\n       </span>\n       ) along with three short vowels\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Near-open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open front unrounded vowel">\n         \xc3\xa6\n        </a>\n        /\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /i/\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /u/\n       </span>\n       . At some point prior to the 16th century in the general area now modern Iran,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /e\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /i\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       merged into\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /i\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       , and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /o\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /u\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       merged into\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /u\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       . Thus, older contrasts such as\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xb4\xdb\x8c\xd8\xb1\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        sh\xc4\x93r\n       </i>\n       "lion" vs.\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xb4\xdb\x8c\xd8\xb1\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        sh\xc4\xabr\n       </i>\n       "milk", and\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xb2\xd9\x88\xd8\xaf\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        z\xc5\xabd\n       </i>\n       "quick" vs\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xb2\xd9\x88\xd8\xb1\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        z\xc5\x8dr\n       </i>\n       "strong" were lost. However, there are exceptions to this rule, and in some words,\n       <i>\n        \xc4\x93\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        \xc5\x8d\n       </i>\n       are preserved\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       or merged into the diphthongs\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        [e\xc9\xaa]\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        [o\xca\x8a]\n       </span>\n       (which are descendants of the diphthongs\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        [\xc3\xa6\xc9\xaa]\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        [\xc3\xa6\xca\x8a]\n       </span>\n       in Early New Persian), instead of merging into\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /i\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /u\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       . Examples of the exception can be found in words such as\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xb1\xd9\x88\xd8\xb4\xd9\x86\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        [ro\xca\x8a\xca\x83\xc3\xa6n]\n       </span>\n       (bright).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       However, in Dari, the archaic distinction of\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /e\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /i\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       (respectively known as\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xdb\x8c\xd8\xa7\xdb\x8c \xd9\x85\xd8\xac\xd9\x87\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        Y\xc4\x81-ye majh\xc5\xabl\n       </i>\n       and\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xdb\x8c\xd8\xa7\xdb\x8c \xd9\x85\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb1\xd9\x88\xd9\x81\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        Y\xc4\x81-ye ma\'r\xc5\xabf\n       </i>\n       ) is still preserved as well as the distinction of\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /o\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /u\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       (known as\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x88 \xd9\x85\xd8\xac\xd9\x87\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        W\xc4\x81w-e majh\xc5\xabl\n       </i>\n       and\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x88 \xd9\x85\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb1\xd9\x88\xd9\x81\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        W\xc4\x81w-e ma\'r\xc5\xabf\n       </i>\n       ). On the other hand, in standard Tajik, the length distinction has disappeared, and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /i\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       merged with\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /i/\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /u\xcb\x90/\n       </span>\n       with\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /u/\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Therefore, contemporary Afghan Dari dialects are the closest to the vowel inventory of Early New Persian.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to most studies on the subject (e.g. Samareh 1977, Pisowicz 1985, Najafi 2001), the three vowels traditionally considered long (\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /i/\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /u/\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\xc9\x92/\n       </span>\n       ) are currently distinguished from their short counterparts (\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /e/\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /o/\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\xc3\xa6/\n       </span>\n       ) by position of articulation rather than by length. However, there are studies (e.g. Hayes 1979, Windfuhr 1979) that consider vowel length to be the active feature of the system, with\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\xc9\x92/\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /i/\n       </span>\n       , and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /u/\n       </span>\n       phonologically long or bimoraic and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\xc3\xa6/\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /e/\n       </span>\n       , and\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /o/\n       </span>\n       phonologically short or monomoraic.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are also some studies that consider quality and quantity to be both active in the Iranian system (such as Toosarvandani 2004). That offers a synthetic analysis including both quality and quantity, which often suggests that Modern Persian vowels are in a transition state between the quantitative system of Classical Persian and a hypothetical future Persian, which will eliminate all traces of quantity and retain quality as the only active feature.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The length distinction is still strictly observed by careful reciters of classic-style poetry for all varieties (including Tajik).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants">\n        Consonants\n     </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Labial_consonant"    </a>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n          <a        h\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Trill_consonant" title="Trill consonant">\n          Trill\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n          <a class="mw-redirect" </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">\n          Approximant\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n          <a <td>\n         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n          <a href="/wiki/Palatal_approximant#Palatal" title="Palatal approximant">\n           j\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">\n        Grammar\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Grammar">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_grammar" title="Persian grammar">\n        Persian grammar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Morphology">\n        Morphology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Morphology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Suffixes predominate Persian\n       <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(linguistics)" title="Morphology (linguistics)">\n        morphology\n       </a>\n       , though there are a small number of prefixes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-megerdoomian2000_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-megerdoomian2000-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Verbs can express tense and\n       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_aspect" title="Grammatical aspect">\n        aspect\n       </a>\n       , and they agree with the subject in person and number.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mahootian1997_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mahootian1997-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There is no\n       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">\n        grammatical gender\n       </a>\n       in Persian, and pronouns are not marked for\n       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender#Grammatical_vs._natural_gender" title="Grammatical gender">\n        natural gender\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Syntax">\n        Syntax\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Syntax">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Normal declarative sentences are structured as\n       <i>\n        (S) (PP) (O) V\n       </i>\n       : sentences have optional\n       <a href="/wiki/Subject_(grammar)" title="Subject (grammar)">\n        subjects\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prepositional_phrase" title="Prepositional phrase">\n        prepositional phrases\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Object_(grammar)" title="Object (grammar)">\n        objects\n       </a>\n       followed by a compulsory\n       <a href="/wiki/Verb" title="Verb">\n        verb\n       </a>\n       . If the object is specific, the object is followed by the word\n       <i>\n        r\xc4\x81\n       </i>\n       and precedes prepositional phrases:\n       <i>\n        (S) (O +\n       </i>\n       r\xc4\x81\n       <i>\n        ) (PP) V\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mahootian1997_80-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mahootian1997-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">\n        Vocabulary\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Vocabulary">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_vocabulary" title="Persian vocabulary">\n        Persian vocabulary\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Native_word_formation">\n        Native word formation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Native word formation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Persian makes extensive use of word building and combining affixes, stems, nouns and adjectives. Persian frequently uses derivational\n       <a href="/wiki/Agglutination" title="Agglutination">\n        agglutination\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Word_formation" title="Word formation">\n        form new words\n       </a>\n       from nouns, adjectives, and verbal stems. New words are extensively formed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Compound_(linguistics)" title="Compound (linguistics)">\n        compounding\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 two existing words combining into a new one, as is common in\n       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">\n        German\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">\n        Influences\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Influences">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_words_of_Persian_origin" title="List of English words of Persian origin">\n        List of English words of Persian origin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_French_loanwords_in_Persian" title="List of French loanwords in Persian">\n        List of French loanwords in Persian\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages#Comparison_table_of_the_Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">\n        Iranian languages \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Comparison table of the Iranian languages\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       While having a lesser influence on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nushin_Namazi_19-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Nushin_Namazi-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and other languages of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">\n        Mesopotamia\n       </a>\n       and its core vocabulary being of\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Persian" title="Middle Persian">\n        Middle Persian\n       </a>\n       origin,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richard_Davis_2006._pp._602-603_13-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Richard_Davis_2006._pp._602-603-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New Persian contains a considerable amount of Arabic lexical items,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lazard_10-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lazard-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lazard.2C_Gilbert_1971_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lazard.2C_Gilbert_1971-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Classe_2000_1057_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Classe_2000_1057-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which were Persianized\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lambtonexcerpt_21-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lambtonexcerpt-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and often took a different meaning and usage than the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       original. Persian loanwords of Arabic origin especially include\n       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">\n        Islamic\n       </a>\n       terms. The Arabic vocabulary in other Iranian, Turkic and Indic languages is generally understood to have been copied from New Persian, not from Arabic itself.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       John R. Perry, in his article\n       <i>\n        Lexical Areas and Semantic Fields of Arabic\n       </i>\n       , estimates that about 24 percent of an everyday vocabulary of 20,000 words in current Persian, and more than 25 percent of the vocabulary of classical and modern Persian literature, are of Arabic origin. The text frequency of these loan words is generally lower and varies by style and topic area. It may approach 25 percent of a text in literature.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perry_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Perry-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Among the Arabic loan words, relatively few (14 percent) are from the semantic domain of material culture, while a larger number are from domains of intellectual and spiritual life.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Most of the Arabic words used in Persian are either synonyms of native terms or could be glossed in Persian.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The inclusion of Mongolian and Turkic elements in the Persian language should also be mentioned,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       not only because of the political role a succession of Turkic dynasties played in Iranian history, but also because of the immense prestige Persian language and literature enjoyed in the wider (non-Arab) Islamic world, which was often ruled by sultans and emirs with a Turkic background. The Turkish and Mongolian vocabulary in Persian is minor in comparison to that of Arabic and these words were mainly confined to military, pastoral terms and political sector (titles, administration, etc.).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New military and political titles were coined based partially on Middle Persian (e.g.\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb4\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        arte\xc5\xa1\n       </i>\n       for "army", instead of the Uzbek\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd9\x82\xd8\xa4\xd8\xb4\xdb\x8c\xd9\x86\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        qo\xca\xbbshin\n       </i>\n       ;\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xb3\xd8\xb1\xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xda\xa9\xd8\xb1\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        sarla\xc5\xa1kar\n       </i>\n       ;\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xaf\xd8\xb1\xdb\x8c\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        dary\xc4\x81b\xc4\x81n\n       </i>\n       ; etc.) in the 20th century. Persian has likewise influenced the vocabularies of other languages, especially other\n       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">\n        Indo-European languages\n       </a>\n       such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">\n        Armenian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Urdu, and (to a lesser extent) Hindi; the latter two through conquests of Persianized Central Asian Turkic and Afghan invaders;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">\n        Turkic languages\n       </a>\n       such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">\n        Ottoman Turkish\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_language" title="Chagatai language">\n        Chagatai\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tatar_language" title="Tatar language">\n        Tatar\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">\n        Turkish\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">\n        Turkmen\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azeri_language" title="Azeri language">\n        Azeri\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">\n        Uzbek\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Karachay-Balkar_language" title="Karachay-Balkar language">\n        Karachay-Balkar\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Compendium_of_the_World_Languages_91-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Compendium_of_the_World_Languages-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caucasian_languages" title="Caucasian languages">\n        Caucasian languages\n       </a>\n       such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">\n        Georgian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and to a lesser extent,\n       <a href="/wiki/Avar_language" title="Avar language">\n        Avar\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lezgin_language" title="Lezgin language">\n        Lezgin\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Afro-Asiatic languages like\n       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Neo-Aramaic" title="Assyrian Neo-Aramaic">\n        Assyrian\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_loanwords_in_Assyrian_Neo-Aramaic" title="List of loanwords in Assyrian Neo-Aramaic">\n        List of loanwords in Assyrian Neo-Aramaic\n       </a>\n       ) and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and even\n       <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_languages" title="Dravidian languages">\n        Dravidian languages\n       </a>\n       indirectly especially\n       <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">\n        Telugu\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Brahui_language" title="Brahui language">\n        Brahui\n       </a>\n       ; as well as\n       <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">\n        Austronesian languages\n       </a>\n       such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">\n        Indonesian\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">\n        Malay\n       </a>\n       . Persian has also had a significant lexical influence, via Turkish, on\n       <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">\n        Albanian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">\n        Serbian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">\n        Croatian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">\n        Bosnian\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian" title="Serbo-Croatian">\n        Serbo-Croatian\n       </a>\n       , particularly as spoken in\n       <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">\n        Bosnia and Herzegovina\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Use of occasional foreign synonyms instead of Persian words can be a common practice in everyday communications as an alternative expression. In some instances in addition to the Persian vocabulary, the equivalent synonyms from multiple foreign languages can be used. For example, in Iranian colloquial Persian (not in Afghanistan or Tajikistan), the phrase "thank you" may be expressed using the French word\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd9\x85\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb3\xdb\x8c\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        merci\n       </i>\n       (stressed, however, on the first syllable), the hybrid Persian-Arabic phrase\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaliq">\n        \xd9\x85\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb4\xda\xa9\xd9\x91\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x85\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        mote\xc5\xa1akker am\n       </i>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami \xe2\x80\x8e\n       <i>\n        mote\xc5\xa1akker\n       </i>\n       being "merciful" in Arabic, commonly pronounced\n       <i>\n        mot\xc4\x8dakker\n       </i>\n       in Persian, and the verb\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\',  am\n       </i>\n       meaning "I am" in Persian), or by the pure Persian phrase\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel am\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">\n        Orthography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Orthography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" (Persian) proportion rules.\n         <sup class="reference" id="ref__Smith1989_a">\n          <a href="#endnote_Smith1989_a">\n           [ 1 ]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n Ali-Akbar Dehkhoda\n         </a>\n         \'s personal handwriting, a typical\n         <a href="/wiki/Cursive" title="Cursive">\n          cursive\n         </a>\n         Persian script.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_word_Persian_in_Pahlavi_script.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="53" data-file-width="140" height="53" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/de/The_word_Persian_in_Pahlavi_script.png" width="140"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_word_Persian_in_Pahlavi_script.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The word Persian in\n         <a href="/wiki/Pahlavi_scripts" title="Pahlavi scripts">\n          Pahlavi scripts\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The vast majority of modern Iranian Persian and Dari text is written with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">\n        Arabic script\n       </a>\n       . Tajiki, which is considered by some linguists to be a Persian dialect influenced by\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">\n        Turkic languages\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">\n        Central Asia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perry2005_95-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-perry2005-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lazard1956_96-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lazard1956-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is written with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">\n        Cyrillic script\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">\n        Tajikistan\n       </a>\n       (see\n       <a href="/wiki/Tajik_alphabet" title="Tajik alphabet">\n        Tajik alphabet\n       </a>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Persian_alphabet">\n        Persian alphabet\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Persian alphabet">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_alphabet" title="Persian alphabet">\n        Persian alphabet\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Modern Iranian Persian and Afghan Persian are written using a modified variant of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic_alphabet" title="Arabic alphabet">\n        Arabic alphabet\n       </a>\n       , which uses different pronunciation and additional letters not found in Arabic. Tajik Persian, as used in Tajikistan, is typically written in a modified version of the Cyrillic script. There also exist several\n       <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Persian" title="Romanization of Persian">\n        romanization systems for Persian\n       </a>\n       . After the\n       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia" title="Muslim conquest of Persia">\n        Muslim conquest of Persia\n       </a>\n       , it took approximately 150 years before Persians adopted the Arabic script in place of the older alphabet. Previously, two different scripts were used,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pahlavi_scripts" title="Pahlavi scripts">\n        Pahlavi\n       </a>\n       , used for Middle Persian, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Avestan_alphabet" title="Avestan alphabet">\n        Avestan alphabet\n       </a>\n       (in Persian, D\xc4\xabndapirak or Din Dabire\xe2\x80\x94literally: religion script), used for religious purposes, primarily for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Avestan" title="Avestan">\n        Avestan\n       </a>\n       but sometimes for Middle Persian.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the modern Persian script,\n       <a href="/wiki/Vowel_length" title="Vowel length">\n        historically short vowels\n       </a>\n       are usually not written, only the historically long ones are represented in the text, so words distinguished from each other only by short vowels are ambiguous in writing: Western Persian\n       <i>\n        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Persian transliteration">\n         kerm\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       "worm",\n       <i>\n        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Persian transliteration">\n         karam\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       "generosity",\n       <i>\n        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Persian transliteration">\n         kerem\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       "cream", and\n       <i>\n        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Persian transliteration">\n         krom\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       "chrome" are all spelled\n       <i>\n        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Persian transliteration">\n         krm\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xda\xa9\xd8\xb1\xd9\x85\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e) in Persian. The reader must determine the word from context. The Arabic system of vocalization marks known as\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harakat" title="Harakat">\n         harakat\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       is also used in Persian, although some of the symbols have different pronunciations. For example, a\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%E1%B8%8Cammah" title="\xe1\xb8\x8cammah">\n         \xe1\xb8\x8dammah\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       is pronounced\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        [\xca\x8a~u]\n       </span>\n       , while in Iranian Persian it is pronounced\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        [o]\n       </span>\n       . This system is not used in mainstream Persian literature; it is primarily used for teaching and in some (but not all) dictionaries.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are several letters generally only used in Arabic loanwords. These letters are pronounced the same as similar Persian letters. For example, there are four functionally identical letters for\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_fricative#Voiced_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiced alveolar fricative">\n         z\n        </a>\n        /\n       </span>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xb2 \xd8\xb0 \xd8\xb6 \xd8\xb8\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e), three letters for\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_fricative#Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar fricative">\n         s\n        </a>\n        /\n       </span>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xb3 \xd8\xb5 \xd8\xab\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e), two letters for\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_and_alveolar_stops#Alveolar" title="Voiceless dental and alveolar stops">\n         t\n        </a>\n        /\n       </span>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xb7 \xd8\xaa\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e), two letters for\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_glottal_fricative" title="Voiceless glottal fricative">\n         h\n        </a>\n        /\n       </span>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xad \xd9\x87\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e). On the other hand, there are four letters that don\'t exist in Arabic\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd9\xbe \xda\x86 \xda\x98 \xda\xaf\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Additions">\n        Additions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Additions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_alphabet" title="Persian alphabet">\n        Persian alphabet\n       </a>\n       adds four letters to the Arabic alphabet:\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto; text-align:center;">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Sound\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Isolated form\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Name\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n          /p/\n         </span>\n        </td>\n        <td style="font-size: larger">\n         <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n          \xda\x98\n         </span>\n         \xe2\x80\x8e\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <i>\n          \xc5\xbee (zhe or jhe)\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n          /\xc9\xa1/\n         </span>\n        </td>\n        <td style="font-size: larger">\n         <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n          \xda\xaf\n         </span>\n         \xe2\x80\x8e\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <i>\n          ge (g\xc4\x81f)\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Historically, there was used also a special letter for the sound\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        /\xce\xb2/\n       </span>\n       . This letter is used no more as the /\xce\xb2/-sound changed to /b/, i.e. archaic \xd8\xb2\xda\xa4\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 /za\xce\xb2\xc4\x81n/ &gt; \xd8\xb2\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 /z\xc3\xa6b\xc9\x92n/ \'language\'\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto; text-align:center;">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Sound\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Isolated form\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Name\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n          /\xce\xb2/\n         </span>\n        </td>\n        <td style="font-size: larger">\n         <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n          \xda\xa4\n         </span>\n         \xe2\x80\x8e\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <i>\n          \xce\xb2e\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Variations">\n        Variations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Variations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The Persian alphabet also modifies some letters of the Arabic alphabet. For example,\n       <i>\n        alef with hamza below\n       </i>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl">\n        \xd8\xa5\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\xc2\xa0) changes to\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Aleph" title="Aleph">\n         alef\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd8\xa7\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\xc2\xa0); words using various\n       <a href="/wiki/Hamza" title="Hamza">\n        hamzas\n       </a>\n       get spelled with yet another kind of hamza (so that\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd9\x85\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa4\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e becomes\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'IranNastaliq\', \'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Persian Nastaliq">\n        \xd9\x85\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa6\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e) even though the latter is also correct in Arabic; and\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teh_marbuta" title="Teh marbuta">\n         teh marbuta\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl">\n        \xd8\xa9\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\xc2\xa0) changes to\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/He_(letter)" title="He (letter)">\n         heh\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu\', \'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft\', \'Hussaini Nastaleeq\', \'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq\', IranNastaliq, \'Awami Nastaliq\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta3\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta2\', \'Awami Nastaliq Beta1\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq\', \'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01\', \'Pak Nastaleeq\', \'PDMS_Jauhar\', \'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq\';" title="Nastaliq">\n        \xd9\x87\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x8e\xc2\xa0) or\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taw_(letter)" title="Taw (letter)">\n         teh\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (\n       <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: \'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq\', \'Urdu Typesetting\', \'Noto \xe2\x80\x8e\xc2\xa0).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The letters different in shape are:\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto; text-align:center;">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Arabic Style letter\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Persian Style letter\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         name\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td        <td>\n         <i>\n          ye\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_alphabet">\n        Latin alphabet\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Latin alphabet">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Persian" title="Romanization of Persian">\n        Romanization of Persian\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">\n        International Organization for Standardization\n       </a>\n       has published a standard for simplified\n       <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">\n        transliteration\n       </a>\n       of Persian into Latin, ISO 233-3, titled "Information and documentation\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 Transliteration of Arabic characters into Latin characters\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 Part 3: Persian language\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 Simplified transliteration"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but the transliteration scheme is not in widespread use.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another Latin alphabet, based on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_Turkic_Alphabet#In_the_USSR" title="Common Turkic Alphabet">\n        Common Turkic Alphabet\n       </a>\n       , was used in\n       <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">\n        Tajikistan\n       </a>\n       in the 1920s and 1930s. The alphabet was phased out in favor of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tajik_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Tajik Cyrillic alphabet">\n        Cyrillic\n       </a>\n       in the late 1930s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perry2005_95-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-perry2005-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fingilish" title="Fingilish">\n        Fingilish\n       </a>\n       is Persian using\n       <a href="/wiki/ISO_basic_Latin_alphabet" title="ISO basic Latin alphabet">\n        ISO basic Latin alphabet\n       </a>\n       . It is most commonly used in\n       <a href="/wiki/Online_chat" title="Online chat">\n        chat\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Email" title="Email">\n        emails\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short_Message_Service" title="Short Message Service">\n        SMS\n       </a>\n       applications. The orthography is not standardized, and varies among writers and even media (for example, typing \'aa\' for the\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        [\xc9\x92]\n       </span>\n       phoneme is easier on computer keyboards than on cellphone keyboards, resulting in smaller usage of the combination on cellphones).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tajik_alphabet">\n        Tajik alphabet\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Tajik alphabet">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Akademijai_ilmxhoi_jumxhurii_tojikiston.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="288" data-file-width="612" height="104" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Akademijai_ilmxhoi_jumxhurii_tojikiston.jpg/220px-Akademijai_ilmxhoi_jumxhurii_tojikiston.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Akademijai_ilmxhoi_jumxhurii_tojikiston.jpg/330px-Akademijai_ilmxhoi_jumxhurii_tojikiston.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Akademijai_ilmxhoi_jumxhurii_tojikiston.jpg/440px-Akademijai_ilmxhoi_jumxhurii_tojikiston.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akademijai_ilmxhoi_jumxhurii_tojikiston.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Tajiki advertisement for an academy.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Tajik_alphabet" title="Tajik alphabet">\n        Tajik alphabet\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Cyrillic script was introduced for writing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">\n        Tajik language\n       </a>\n       under the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tajik_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic">\n        Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic\n       </a>\n       in the late 1930s, replacing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tajik_alphabet#Transliteration_standards" title="Tajik alphabet">\n        Latin alphabet\n       </a>\n       that had been used since the\n       <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">\n        October Revolution\n       </a>\n       and the Persian script that had been used earlier. After 1939, materials published in Persian in the Persian script were banned from the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perry2005_95-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-perry2005-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Examples">\n        Examples\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Examples">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The following text is from Article 1 of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">\n        Universal Declaration of Human Rights\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <table </span>\n        </li>\n        <li id="cite_note-Lazard-10">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          ^\n          <a href="#cite_ref-Lazard_10-0">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              a\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n          <a href="#cite_ref-Lazard_10-1">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              b\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n          <a href="#cite_ref-Lazard_10-2">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n
